Based on the comparison plots, I notice that the model     
struggles to capture some of the longer-term dynamics,     
particularly in nutrient cycling. I propose adding light   
limitation to phytoplankton growth, as this is a crucial   
environmental factor that can significantly affect primary 
production patterns.                                       

Let's modify the model to include light limitation using a 
simple light attenuation model where light decreases with  
increasing phytoplankton biomass (self-shading effect).    

Here are the proposed changes:

 <<<<<<< SEARCH                                            
 =======                                                   
 \section{Model Enhancement: Light Limitation}             
                                                           
 The original NPZ model has been enhanced to include light 
 limitation effects on phytoplankton growth. This          
 modification addresses a key environmental driver of      
 phytoplankton dynamics that was previously missing from t 
 model.                                                    
                                                           
 \subsection{Ecological Justification}                     
 Light availability is crucial for photosynthesis and      
 therefore directly impacts phytoplankton growth. As       
 phytoplankton populations increase, they create           
 self-shading effects that can limit light penetration to  
 deeper waters, creating a natural negative feedback       
 mechanism. This addition helps explain:                   
                                                           
 1. The observed limitation in peak phytoplankton biomass  
 2. More realistic nutrient uptake patterns                
 3. Better representation of the system's carrying capacit 
                                                           
 \subsection{Mathematical Implementation}                  
 The light limitation is implemented using:                
 \begin{itemize}                                           
     \item Beer-Lambert law for light attenuation: $I = I_ 
 e^{-P}$                                                   
     \item Michaelis-Menten kinetics for light limitation: 
 $f(I) = \frac{I}{K_I + I}$                                
     \item Combined with existing nutrient limitation:     
 $\text{Growth} = r_{max} \cdot \frac{N}{K_N + N} \cdot    
 \frac{I}{K_I + I} \cdot P$                                
 \end{itemize}                                             
                                                           
 This formulation creates a more mechanistic representatio 
 of phytoplankton growth limitations, potentially improvin 
 the model's ability to capture observed patterns in the   
 data.                                                     
 >>>>>>> REPLACE                                           
                                                           

These changes introduce light limitation while keeping the 
model relatively simple. The self-shading effect provides  
an additional feedback mechanism that could help explain   
some of the observed patterns in the data, particularly the
limitation of peak phytoplankton biomass and the subsequent
nutrient dynamics.
